commit 55d0e441f0ee2a1ca9ee751ab7d81b67995e170a
Author: muzimuzhi <muzimuzhi@gmail.com>
Date:   Thu Oct 13 17:03:42 2022 +0800

    docs: use handler `/.append`
    
    to avoid a subtle constraint of `/.add` that
        /.add={<arg1>}{<arg2>}  % and
        /.add={<arg1>} {<arg2>}
    are different and the second is, in most cases, wrong usage.
    
    Signed-off-by: muzimuzhi <muzimuzhi@gmail.com>

commit 1dbf7ae5ddd5479e8a046d76d49c7bfd001e5f0a
Author: Henri Menke <henri@henrimenke.de>
Date:   Sun Jan 30 10:10:53 2022 +0100

    fix!(pgfkeys): more careful treatment of \relax in pgfkeys
    
    There are a lot of instances in pgfkeys where \csname is used, e.g. in
    \pgfkeysgetvalueof. This will \let the mentioned csname become \relax so we have
    to be prepared for this in across the board in pgfkeys. Indeed, this was the
    original behavior before eTeX but it somehow got lost when transitioning to
    \ifcsname. The behavior is broken with eTeX since 641a8832.
    
    BREAKING CHANGE: \pgfkeysvalueof will expand to an alias for the primitve \relax
    in case the key was undefined rather than to a \relaxed csname.
    
    Co-authored-by: Jonathan Spratte <jspratte@yahoo.de>
    Co-authored-by: muzimuzhi <muzimuzhi@gmail.com>
    Signed-off-by: Henri Menke <henri@henrimenke.de>

commit 00ef2e1f6f7ff70c1a1b0f586b3fc07189c992e6
Author: muzimuzhi <muzimuzhi@gmail.com>
Date:   Sat Dec 11 04:08:01 2021 +0800

    fix(animations): Add missing `\pgf@sys@tonumber` before `<dimen>`
    
    "Private" implementations of `pgfmath` functions only accept unit-less
    numbers as their arguments, e.g.,
        \pgfmathadd@{1.0}{1.0}
    So every dimension used as their argument must be prefixed by a `\pgf@sys@tonumber`, e.g.,
        \pgfmathadd@{\pgf@sys@tonumber\pgf@x}{\pgf@sys@tonumber\pgf@y}
    
    This eliminates "Missing character" reports for `p` and `t`.
    
    Signed-off-by: muzimuzhi <muzimuzhi@gmail.com>

commit 38c3df2548b7a81bc70df6edcecaec0c5dd50167
Merge: a0d9cada fcc2b3f4
Author: Henri Menke <henri@henrimenke.de>
Date:   Fri Oct 8 12:57:29 2021 +0200

    Merge pull request #1056 from schtandard/pgfcalendarifdate_cleanup
    
    Avoid spurious tokens in \pgfcalendarifdate expansion

commit fcc2b3f4d895fe2996325d18b0dadfbeaf4f6a6e
Author: BeneIII <benedikt.wilde@uni-tuebingen.de>
Date:   Fri Oct 8 12:47:20 2021 +0200

    Avoid spurious tokens in \pgfcalendarifdate expansion
    
    Just like other similar macros in LaTeX, \pgfcalendarifdate should avoid
    inserting tokens (namely \else of \if) behind its result. For example
    \pgfcalendarifdate{\today}{Sunday}{\textbf}{\textit}{Some text}
    should apply \textbf to {Some text} on Sundays and \textit on all other
    days. The unexpected extra tokens would get in the way.
    
    Signed-off-by: BeneIII <benedikt.wilde@uni-tuebingen.de>

commit 3abc90c30c489966f9d717fb86a9fb037241121b
Author: Mario Frasca <mariotomo@gmail.com>
Date:   Wed Aug 11 04:25:40 2021 -0500

    add rhombic polihedra (#1022)
    
    * adds rhombi faces, two rhombic dodecahedra, partial tricontahedron.
    
    the rhombi faces are four: right or left leaning, golden or square-of-two
    ratio between diagonals.  there's the "type 1" rhombic dodecahedron, a
    Catalan solid having as faces square-of-two rhombi, the "type 2" rhombic
    dodecahedron having as faces golden rhombi, and about half the faces needed
    to build a golden rhombic tricontahedron.
    
    * fixing tricontahedron to use golden rhombi
    
    * addresses #1020, refinements on flat golden rhombic dodecahedron
    
    * addresses #1020, added "type 1" specification
    
    * reviewing, adding to the manual page.

commit ebe3b701540895a956a7e4f07e9c3abf6c718f18
Author: Joel Coffman <joelcoffman@gmail.com>
Date:   Sat Jul 31 05:46:51 2021 -0600

    Add reference for transform key
    
    The description of the `text along path' decoration mentions using the
    `transform` key to move text vertically (relative to the baseline).
    Unfortunately, "transform" appears more than 1000 times in the
    documentation, which makes finding the relevant documentation for that
    key difficult, as evidenced personally and a question on TeX - LaTeX
    Stack Exchange that addresses this issue.
    
    This change adds a reference to the appropriate section in the
    documentation for the `/pgf/decoration/transform` key so that future
    users don't have this same difficulty. (It effectively follows the
    recommendation in the answer to the TeX - LaTeX Stack Exchange
    question, which has not been done in the intervening eight years.)
    
    How can I move a "text along path" vertically? (TeX - LaTeX Stack
    Exchange): https://tex.stackexchange.com/a/134589

commit 49d54fb06bfe4e38c8ce156cb399663cd68df0c7
Author: Michal Hoftich <michal.h21@gmail.com>
Date:   Sun Apr 11 16:20:02 2021 +0200

    Update pgfsys-dvisvgm4ht.def
    
    Here is updated version of the TeX4ht dvisvgm driver. It fixes some bugs and provides two modes. The default mode loads `dvips` specials. It works in most cases, but it fails sometimes. For example with [patterns](https://tex.stackexchange.com/q/590599/2891). The second mode loads `dvisvgm` specials. It fixes the pattern sample, but it fails for   [other examples](https://texample.net/tikz/examples/poincare/). All text labels are put at one place. This `dvisvgm` mode can be required using
    
          make4ht filename.tex "tikz+"

commit de0c5f4416aa1e691cb255cb19fd1bc95fce0a0a
Author: Joel Coffman <8376231+joel-coffman@users.noreply.github.com>
Date:   Sat Feb 13 14:24:48 2021 -0700

    Correct documentation for .code 2 args second arg
    
    The current documentation states that the key handler `.code 2 args`
    treats the second argument as optional, but the implementation
    differs: if the second argument isn't provided, then the first letter
    of the first argument is treated as the first argument, and the
    remainder of the first argument is treated as the second argument.
    Thus, this change removes the incorrect statement from the
    documentation.
    
    Closes #991

    [doc] pgfkeys: unify order of ".code" and ".style"
    
    ".code" handlers are documented in order
        simple, 2 args, n args, args, add, prefix, append
    while ".style" ones have "args" documented before "n args". This commit
    unifies the order of ".style" to that of ".code".

commit 908db0011cc96b4092b45de7d432e3ead32f4323
Author: Henri Menke <henrimenke@gmail.com>
Date:   Tue Jul 7 18:24:14 2020 +1200

    Invert transform before assigning intersection #889
    
    This will always return the intersection in the untransformed scope, so
    it is necessary to apply the same transformation as was active when
    `\pgfintersectionofpaths' was called, although that should be the case
    most of the time.

commit 71becc1833143d2ccb7b7e9b5b003b1ad0b6c10c
Author: muzimuzhi <muzimuzhi@gmail.com>
Date:   Thu Sep 3 22:33:25 2020 +0800

    pgfsys-xetex: sync with upstream, #909
    
    There was a "\pdfsavepos" bug in XeTeX
        https://sourceforge.net/p/xetex/bugs/56/
    which caused the asymmetric workaround "\pgfqpoint{2\hoffset}{0pt}"
    in defining node "current page". XeTeX has fixed the bug in 0.999992
    hence now pgf can use a normal symmetric
    "\pgfqpoint{\hoffset}{\voffset}".

commit 494bd677709b9f2eb938d96eeb0c2ad29ae37aa3
Author: Henri Menke <henrimenke@gmail.com>
Date:   Tue May 26 14:36:36 2020 +1200

    New key `/pgf/fpu/install only' #861
    
    This key will selectively install the specified functions from the fpu
    library to be able to avoid `Dimension too large' errors in specific
    cases.  Be aware that under certain circumstances the fpu comes with a
    loss of precision due to the underlying fixed-point arithmetic of TeX.
    These situations are rare but have be looked out for.
    
    [[ Example: In general the fpu increases the range of permissible number
                substantially but sometimes has precision problems.
    
        \usetikzlibrary{fpu}
        \pgfkeys{/pgf/fpu/install only={divide}}
        \pgfmathparse{12.34/0.001234}\pgfmathresult % 10000.000000 (good)
        \pgfmathparse{12/4}\pgfmathresult % 2.9999000000000 (bad)
    
    ]]

commit 8095bc5705616236533cf9bd069ff0ec50e71c94
Author: Henri Menke <henrimenke@gmail.com>
Date:   Mon May 18 22:49:43 2020 +1200

    If prefixed name does not exist, look up global name #846
    
    We had similar things already.  Usually, when a prefixed name does not
    exist TikZ either bails or just does nothing.  Here we have the latter
    kind.  If the prefixed node has no anchor, TikZ just does nothing and
    leaves \tikz@shapeborder@name unset.  This has adverse effects when
    drawing edges, because they store the node name and restore it later.
    When the node name is restored, another name prefix is added to the
    already prefixed node that was stored.  To remedy this, we now try the
    unprefixed node, when the prefixed node does not exist.  This is
    probably not 100% compatible but whoever was relying on this behavior
    was on thin ice anyway.  The new behavior is more of the kind of “do
    what I mean”.

Author: Henri Menke <henri@icp.uni-stuttgart.de>
Date:   Thu Jan 16 19:19:50 2020 +1300

    Address the CTAN issues #816
    
    Copyrights were updated automatically by querying the last time the file
    was touched in the Git repo and replacing the notice accordingly.
    
    for file in $(git ls-files); do
        year="$(git log -1 --pretty="format:%cI" -- "${file}" | cut -d'-' -f 1)"
        sed -i "s/^% Copyright\(.*\)20[0-9][0-9]/% Copyright\1${year}/" "${file}"
    done

commit 88951be592b558b94b14a97aaffe9df6c1ce61ee
Author: Henri Menke <henri@icp.uni-stuttgart.de>
Date:   Mon Nov 4 14:45:05 2019 +1300

    Fix `name prefix' for pics
    
    There were two issues:
    
    1. Pile-up of `name prefix' #311
    
        There is an extensive and very nice answer on TeX.SX:
        https://tex.stackexchange.com/questions/176900
        I have now implemented the first suggestion of just overriding
        `name prefix'.  I still have to test how this interacts with manual
        setting of `name prefix', but that doesn't seem to be very common
        (at least it doesn't seem to occur in the manual).
    
    2. No resolution of global node names #717
    
        This had the effect that when requesting `current subpath start' (or
        any other global name) from within a pic, the resolution would add
        the prefix and suffix with \tikz@pp@name and if the resulting local
        name was undefined, throw an error.  Now I have implemented a two
        step resolution which first checks whether the local name exists and
        if it doesn't tries the global name.  I hope nobody is relying on
        the fact that before global names weren't resolved.

commit 2b58c0515b431c1061c5044c394ce6d644502180
Author: Henri Menke <henri@icp.uni-stuttgart.de>
Date:   Thu Jul 4 21:25:42 2019 +1200

    \pgfmathrandominteger didn't handle expressions as input
    
    The following example produced spurious .0 in the output because -1 is
    parsed as negation applied to 1 which results in -1.0.  Internally
    \pgfmathrandominteger was using TeX count registers which just stopped
    parsing at the . and left the rest in the output stream.
    
        \input pgf
        \pgfmathparse{random(-1,10)}
        \pgfmathresult
        \bye

commit a310180b4ba32913d14025b9841b2be9fa45cc6c
Author: Henri Menke <henri@icp.uni-stuttgart.de>
Date:   Wed Jun 26 10:13:16 2019 +1200

    Stripping comments was too greedy
    
    The old rule was
    
        \n%%[^\n]*\n
    
    Which matched a newline followed by '%', followed by everything that is
    not a newline, followed by another newline.  The trailing newline was
    the culprit because it consumed the trailing newline, making a comment
    on the next line not a match.  This
    
        % hello
        % world
        % foo
        % bar
    
    transformed into this
    
        % world % bar
    
    because of consuming the trailing newline.  Just leaving it there, i.e.
    
        \n%%[^\n]*
    
    fixes the problem.

commit 0a6f19790dd3a99f8a9a59479416aa21954f7334
Author: Henri Menke <henri@icp.uni-stuttgart.de>
Date:   Wed Jun 26 09:51:27 2019 +1200

    Small fix to the grammar
    
    So far the grammar for key-value list was
    
        list := pair*
        pair := name ( '=' braces )* ','?
    
    Here the parse would fail for things like
    
        width=4cm
    
    because '4cm' does not match the braces rule, so the rule has to be
    adapted to
    
        list := pair*
        pair := name ( '=' ( braces + name ) )* ','?
    
    so that it matches the name rule if the braces rule does not match.
    
    The number of extracted code examples increased rather drastically from
    2128 to 2357.

commit fd9258d8273d46387438ae9ad442e8d24dcd0e71

commit 65b8261c63c6f4adfca60106528e2d1bf1e2cb60
Author: Henri Menke <henri@icp.uni-stuttgart.de>
Date:   Thu Feb 28 18:51:25 2019 +1300

    More accurate \pgfpointnormalised #518 #519 Feature #96
    
    This has been a long-standing problem, that \pgfpointnormalised was too
    inaccurate.  This resulted in wrong intersection points when using the
    projection syntax.  One proposal was to replace the definition of
    \pgfpointnormalised by atan2 and cos and sin.  The prime argument against this
    was the possible performance impact.  This is a reasonable assumption
    considering the large definitions of atan2, cos, and sin.  However, in
    typesetting the manual with the new and the old definition I could only observe
    a 1% performance loss, which corresponds to 4s wallclock time on my machine.
    Since the manual has an enormous amount of TikZ figures on over 1000 pages, I
    think this performance loss can be considered negligible.

commit 31165f2f43d419e1a921a1881bf25743592577a7
Author: Henri Menke <henri@icp.uni-stuttgart.de>
Date:   Mon Feb 4 19:31:03 2019 +1300

    Making the declared coordinate accessible
    
    Often it is desirable to know what was the coordinate that a node (or other
    named thing) was declared with.  This is now made globally available and
    integrated into the let operation under the name \coord.  Keep in mind that
    when calling \coord on something that was not a named thing, you'll just get
    the declared coordinate of the last named thing or \relax if there was nothing
    named before.  [[ Example:
    
        \path (0,0,{cos(45)}) coordinate (A);
        \path let \p1=(A), \p2=(2,2,2) in \pgfextra{\typeout{A=\coord1,B=\coord2}};
    
    will print in the log
    
        A=(0,0,{cos(45)}),B=(0,0,{cos(45)})
    
    because \p2 is not a named coordinate. ]]
    
    Another issue might arise if the shape was not declare with a coordinate at
    all, in which case the result is undefined.  You might end up with the name of
    the thing itself or \relax. [[ Example:
    
        \coordinate (A);
        \path let \p1=(A) in \pgfextra{\typeout{A=\coord1}};
    
    will print in the log
    
        A=(A)
    
    because \p1 was not declare with a coordinate. ]]

commit dda04d3fc57378dcc178f74a8544480af5f2300a
Author: Henri Menke <henri@icp.uni-stuttgart.de>
Date:   Mon Feb 4 19:16:06 2019 +1300

    Globally remember declare coordinate of a node

commit 524e5fbdab0e5450b1ad85aefad721c519feeb19
Author: Henri Menke <henri@icp.uni-stuttgart.de>
Date:   Mon Feb 4 18:26:34 2019 +1300

    Check for \pgfpointxyz before \rawx, \rawy, \rawz

commit 9467c171fe27adb468829f1b196b2b7b5b3a12ba
Author: Henri Menke <henri@icp.uni-stuttgart.de>
Date:   Mon Feb 4 17:54:36 2019 +1300

    Add \rawx, \rawy, \rawz to let operation
    
    There is an issue with 3D coordinates being projected onto the 2D canvas.
    There is not way to reverse the projection because a system of two equations
    (the project 2D coordinates) with three unknowns (the original 3D coordiantes)
    is underdetermined and unsolvable.  Hence I introduce these new little helpers
    which can be used to access the parsed original coordinates.  This works only
    if you use literal coordinates in the let operation, i.e.
    
        \path let \p1=(1,2,3) in ...
    
    will work as expected, but
    
        \coordinate (A) at (1,2,3);
        \path let \p1=(A) in ...
    
    will not work, because the projection has already been performed when defining
    the \coordinate.

    New random number generator
    
    This commit replaces the random number generator (RNG) provided by Lua with the
    one provided by LuaTeX, which is based on the MetaPost RNG.  This has some
    drawbacks and some advantages.
    
    Drawbacks:
    - This will break all documents which are using graphdrawing with force-based
      algorithms right now.  The layout in those algorithms is randomized so the
      final result is quite sensitive to the exact sequence of random numbers.
      This cannot be preserved.
    - The MetaPost RNG is not as well tested as the one provided by Lua.  It might
      have statistical problems and problems with uniformity of random numbers.
      Some of these issues are described in the LaTeX3 random number generation
      documentation.
    
    Advantages:
    - The Lua random number generator is actually platform dependent.  Looking in
      the Lua source code, one can find that when Lua is compiled on POSIX
      platforms, it will use the POSIX random() function, otherwise it will use the
      C standard library rand() function.  The problem with the rand() function is
      that the only requirement is that the random numbers be uniformly
      distributed, no guarantees about their sequence is made.
    - The MetaPost RNG is frozen and will never change.  LuaTeX is frozen as well,
      which means that interfaces will never change.
    - The LuaTeX RNG is already present since version 0.78.3 (5 years old) so
      combined with the previous point, this switch will be both forward- and
      backward-compatible.
    
    The moral of the story is that you should never rely on the exact sequence of
    random numbers.  If you didn't want the sequence to be random, you probably
    shouldn't have used random numbers in the first place.
    
    Related threads on the internet:
    - https://tex.stackexchange.com/questions/468466/tikz-graphdrawing-differences-between-luatex-versions
    - https://tex.stackexchange.com/questions/455001/updated-lualatex-vs-tikz-feynman
    - https://tex.stackexchange.com/questions/467323/wrong-direction-of-vertices-in-tikz-feynman
    - https://github.com/CTeX-org/forum/issues/4

    in pgfplots).

commit 9967f5aae95939ec4fc35b38b7c5e87fb5ba81d0
Author: Jannis Pohlmann <jannis@xfce.org>
Date:   Tue Jul 26 11:29:07 2011 +0000

    graph drawing: Initial work on supporting clusters to be defined.
    
    I'm not entirely happy having a /tikz/graphs/cluster key in
    tikzlibrarygraphdrawing.code.tex, so maybe we can change that later.
    
    This commit introduces a new macro \pgfgdaddnodetocluster{cluster
    name}{node name}. It's name is self-explanatory, I guess. It simply
    calls Interface:addNodeToCluster(node_name, cluster_name) which in turn
    adds the node to the given cluster of the graph.
    The Graph class holds a new clusters array where clusters are stored in
    the order they were defined in TikZ. These clusters can be used for
    implementing constraints for groups of nodes such as placing all nodes
    of a cluster in the same layer of a layered drawing.
    
    This is also what the GansnerKNV1993 node ranking algorithm does now. It
    merges all nodes of a cluster into a single node, re-routes edges as
    necessary and introduces new edges from cluster N to cluster N+1 in
    order to force clusters to be on separate ranks. This is highly
    experimental though. The "modular layered" algorithm now has to remove
    loops and merge multi-edges two times, once before merging clusters and
    once after dissolving clusters again. For this, I added functions in the
    manipulation namespace but this is more of a temporary hack.
    
    The Edge class was reworked a bit internally and now has a new
    Edge:isLoop() method.

    fixed bug in graph viz lib that made it dependent on latex

commit 90f9d34774caa0bbc8e9a66cbfcf244a5c29a878
Author: Jannis Pohlmann <jannis@xfce.org>
Date:   Wed Jul 20 21:01:37 2011 +0000

    graph drawing: Fix bug where loops were re-added too often.

commit e8ef3236d2808d4a3d7c80fa3694f49d77e8fc9e
Author: Jannis Pohlmann <jannis@xfce.org>
Date:   Wed Jul 20 21:01:27 2011 +0000

    graph drawing: Fix coarsening by adding duplicate node/edge checks.
    
    These checks have become necessary now that we no longer avoid duplicate
    nodes and edges in the Graph class. If they were not performed, we'd end
    up with duplicate nodes and edges after interpolating to lesser coarse
    graphs which results in distorted drawings.

commit 61ed4b78a65c58e6de754e69d5d5ede50614f5ff
Author: Jannis Pohlmann <jannis@xfce.org>

    graph drawing: Fix issue in Edge:getNeighbour(). Add Graph:findEdge().

commit c278ef5168786f149859f4e453fab6744f6c19fb
Author: Jannis Pohlmann <jannis@xfce.org>
Date:   Wed Jul 20 21:00:58 2011 +0000

    graph drawing: Never check whether a node/edge exists in a graph/node.
    
    This allows for multi-edges to be created and passed to Lua. Algorithms
    that cannot handle multi-edges need to merge related ones. I guess it
    would be nice to provide standard routines for this (as well as for
    dropping loops).

commit 868a7658c2768e169c8fda164c83de945fc693d9
Author: Jannis Pohlmann <jannis@xfce.org>
Date:   Wed Jul 20 21:00:47 2011 +0000

    graph drawing: Allow multiedges to have a minimum level value of 0.

commit 846540b4cc7506984fb2cf839faa0bf996e55a92
Author: Jannis Pohlmann <jannis@xfce.org>
Date:   Wed Jul 20 21:00:35 2011 +0000

    graph drawing: Rework loop and multiedge handling.
    
    The Edge class no longer checks whether a node is already part of the
    edge. NOTE: This can lead to problems in existing algorithms, so we need
    to verify that those still work.
    
    The result is that loops contain the same node twice. Algorithms can
    detect loops by testing whether tail and head are the same.
    
    The "modular layered" algorithm drops loops prior to the cycle removal
    step and adds them back to the graph before routing the edges. It also
    merges multiedges and restores the original edges prior to the same
    steps as loops.
    
    Again, other algorithms might have to be adjusted to work again (if they
    are broken).

commit e928a8d9805c789175550376b08008427d22a64c
Author: Jannis Pohlmann <jannis@xfce.org>
Date:   Wed Jul 20 21:00:23 2011 +0000

    graph drawing: Fix inf. loop in GansnerKNV1993 crossing minimization.
    
    Two things were buggy here: (1) improvements in the transpose step were
    not always honored as the "improved" flag was overwritten instead of
    performing a logical OR, and (2) positions of nodes in the same rank
    were sometimes switched repeatedly due to checking all neighbours
    instead of just the ones on the next/previous layer (depending on the
    swep direction).

commit b9726065532d9c41db1a174aa74eef606b4aff64
Author: Jannis Pohlmann <jannis@xfce.org>
Date:   Fri Jul 15 23:35:08 2011 +0000

    graph drawing: Add three additional cycle removal heuristics.
    
    These were taken from "Layered Drawings of Digraphs" by Bastert and
    Matuszewski and were named after their original authors.

commit a694b7a830dce22d2fb57c714ac528af540637fe
Author: Jannis Pohlmann <jannis@xfce.org>
Date:   Fri Jul 15 15:53:28 2011 +0000

    graph drawing: Add a modular algorithm for layered graph drawings.
    
    This algorithm is called "modular layered" and uses the different parts
    of the "GansnerKNV1993 layered" algorithm by default. However, it is
    easy to implement alternatives to these default sub-algorithms by
    creating a files like
    
      pgfgd-algorithm-modular-layered-crossing-minimization-MYALGORITHM.lua
    
    or
    
      pgfgd-algorithm-modular-layered-cycle-removal-MYALGORITHM.lua.
    
    Users can then select these by choosing the "modular layered" algorithm
    and setting
    
      /graph drawing/layered drawing/crossing minimization=MYALGORITHM
      /graph drawing/layered drawing/cycle removal=MYALGORITHM.

commit 5e0d5f28a3fabd0f99e34b8acd776d5c6727ad1f
Author: Jannis Pohlmann <jannis@xfce.org>
Date:   Fri Jul 15 15:52:56 2011 +0000

    graph drawing: Add methods for converting between class and file names.
    
    Thes methods make it easier for algorithms to load sub-algorithms by
    providing a consistent way to build their file names and lookup their
    main algorithm class.
    
    In the future, these methods will also be used to load the main
    algorithms. The drawGraphAlgorithm_Foo_bar() functions will be replaced
    by real classes with a :new() and a :run() method.

commit 2c9389ecb05b1794f0a9c59b167be4107536b966
Author: Jannis Pohlmann <jannis@xfce.org>
Date:   Tue Jul 12 22:35:15 2011 +0000

    graph drawing: Reimplement the network simplex using recursive DFS.
    
    This makes it more similar to the original GansnerKNV implementation and
    to the paper. The recursive functions are less error-prone and finally
    work! In future commits I will try to implement 1-2 generic
    pre-/post-order DFS traversals in order to bring iterative DFS back
    without introducing the same weird bugs again that are really hard to
    trace due to the amount of DFS boilerplate code needed.

commit ae915202f67e258497ddf9ca09ef1ec552aa876a
Author: Jannis Pohlmann <jannis@xfce.org>
Date:   Wed Jul 6 21:50:29 2011 +0000

    graph drawing: Fix bugs in NetworkSimplex, Ranking and GansnerKNV.
    
    Ranking normalization used to produce duplicate elements, this is fixed
    now. Also supported now are arbitrary, non-sequential ranks (e.g. -100,
    1, 23, 50 instead of just 0, 1, 2, 3, 4).
    
    This commit also introduces the x coordiante calculation based on the
    network simplex, as proposed by Gansner et al. in their paper. However,
    there still are a few bugs present in our implementation of the
    NetworkSimplex class which lead to assertion failures with some graphs.
    Other graphs, however, already look decent and very similar to the
    layouts produced by GraphViz.

commit beb60c033670e6a651c858d782317964340b1b32
Author: Jannis Pohlmann <jannis@xfce.org>
Date:   Wed Jul 6 21:50:03 2011 +0000

    graph drawing: Parse node box coordinates prior to passing them to Lua.
    
    The TeX box coordinates have the format "123pt" and where passed to Lua
    unmodified before this commit. They are now resolved into point using
    \pgfmathsetmacro and the unit is dropped. As coordinates need to be
    passed back to the TeX layer in their original form, we later append the
    "pt" again.
    
    This fixes Node:getTexWidth() and Node:getTexHeight().

commit a118999593a075eced56b06470e061c9dfb694b0
Author: Jannis Pohlmann <jannis@xfce.org>
Date:   Thu Jun 30 22:35:16 2011 +0000

    graph drawing: Add table.reverse_value_iter(). Use it in NetworkSimplex.
    
    This way, whenever we perform a depth-first search in the network
    simplex algorithm (we need to do this many times in fact), nodes will be
    pushed on the DFS stack in the order they appear in the TikZ code.
    
    The implication on the GansnerKNV layered algorithm is that the edges
    included in the initial spanning tree can be predetermined by writing
    down the desired search paths first and add cross/back edges in TikZ
    afterwards.

    in the GansnerKNV layered algorithm. For this it will have to be made a
    bit more generic though.

commit 38fea1df0b86921d0cb9085d984ac817c48e42a1
Author: Jannis Pohlmann <jannis@xfce.org>
Date:   Tue Jun 28 01:22:04 2011 +0000

    graph drawing: Work on Ranking class and node ordering in GansnerKNV.
    
    The new Ranking class in core/lualayer can be used by all layered
    drawing algorithms in order to manage node ranks and node orderings in
    the different ranks.
    
    The GansnerKNV layered algorithm has been improved to use this new class
    in order to implement node ordering using the heuristic developed by
    Gansner et al that aims at reducing edge crossings in the layered graph
    drawing.

commit c09ff56fddd3b89da2e2fc773abdecda4f3cb440
Author: Jannis Pohlmann <jannis@xfce.org>
Date:   Mon May 30 17:09:26 2011 +0000

    graph drawing:
      - Initial work on layered drawing algorithms (GansnerKNV, Pohlmann).
      - Add algorithm.classify_edges(), an algorithm that performs a depth
        first search on a graph and classifies edges as forward/tree, back
        or cross edges. This can be useful in the cycle removal step of
        layered drawing algorithms as it generates an arc feedback set
        whose reversal preverse the general flow direction of the
        input graph.
      - Fix the first segment of paths with bend points not being rendered
        by prefixing the bend point string with '--' if there is at least
        one bend point.

    Implemented a G_n subgraph for creating grid (or: mesh) graphs.
    This also introduces a new key /tikz/graphs/wrap after=<number> that
    configures how the nodes in such a grid graph are connected. Some of
    the common subgraph keys such as /tikz/graphs/V and /tikz/graphs/n
    can be used with G_n subgraphs as well.
    
    Added a simple grid placement strategy. It currently does not
    support the chain shift and group shift keys properly and does not
    implement any placement order other than left-to-right, so there is
    room for improvement.

commit 8649617556487f555cfa840844d818e369488bf0
Author: Christian Feuersaenger <cfeuersaenger@users.sourceforge.net>
Date:   Mon Dec 29 23:39:35 2008 +0000

    - modified low-level floating point representation. All high level code
    should be completely unaffected; the changes are backwards compatible.
    - Wrote first draft of a floating point unit library (fpu) similar in
    spirit to the fixed point library of Mark Wibrow.
    - Moved all floating point math operations (functions) into the fpu
    library. It is now necessary to include the library in order to use
    floating point math operations. The number formatting methods are still
    available as before.
